## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (classical mechanics) тАФ nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of an oscillator, typically modeled by a second-order ODE x'' = f(x, v, t). With features x (position), v (velocity), and t (time), common models include linear damping/restoring forces, nonlinear stiffness (e.g., Duffing), nonlinear damping (e.g., van der Pol/Rayleigh), and external/parametric periodic forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hooke restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping)
- Damped + constant bias: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 (equilibrium shift / constant external force)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic drag-like damping)
- Coulomb (dry) friction: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Sign(v) (stick-slip / dry friction idealization)
- Simple pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * Sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (angular oscillator with damping)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring)
- Duffing with periodic forcing: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * Cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear resonance)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * Cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-modulated stiffness, Mathieu-type)
- Nonlinear (state-dependent) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (Li├йnard-type damping depending on displacement)
- van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * v**2) * v (velocity-dependent self-excitation)
- Mixed coupling nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * x**2 * v (amplitude-dependent dissipation)
- Anharmonic potential gradient form: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (polynomial approximation to nonlinear restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope тЖТ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects тЖТ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay тЖТ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior тЖТ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects тЖТ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically make dv_dt an odd function of x (e.g., -c*x, -c*sin(c*x), -c*x - c*x^3), reflecting symmetry of the potential about equilibrium.
- Dissipation usually appears as terms odd in v (e.g., -c*v, -c*v*Abs(v), -c*Sign(v)); such terms monotonically remove mechanical energy when no forcing is present.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior is often captured by state-dependent damping that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (1 - c*x^2)*v or (1 - c*v^2)*v, injecting energy at small amplitudes and dissipating it at large amplitudes.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency shifts are commonly modeled by adding odd higher-power stiffness terms (x**3, x**5), producing hardening/softening behavior and nonlinear resonance.
- Explicit periodic dependence on t (Cos(c*t), Sin(c*t)) indicates external driving; this is used to capture resonance peaks, entrainment, and forced responses.
- Parametric resonance is suggested when t-modulation multiplies x (or v), e.g., -(c0 + c1*Cos(c2*t))*x, rather than being added as a pure forcing term.
- Nonlinear damping that depends on x (e.g., (c0 + c1*x**2)*v) often represents geometry/material effects where dissipation increases with displacement amplitude.
- Dry friction models introduce non-smooth terms (Sign(v), Abs(v)), leading to stick-slip and non-sinusoidal waveforms; these structures are key when data show sharp velocity reversals.
- Coupling terms like x*v or x**2*v can indicate energy transfer mechanisms or coordinate-dependent damping, often identifiable when decay rates vary with amplitude.

\[
f(x,t,v)= -0.1430477510\sin(v)\;-\;0.1948307679\,v(1-x^2)\;-\;3.0492397837\,x\,e^{-|x|}
\]
Key structural requirements:
- Has a **\(\sin(v)\)** term with nonzero coefficient.
- Has a **\(v\)** term whose coefficient depends on \(x^2\): \(-0.1948\,v + 0.1948\,v x^2\).
- Has a **non-polynomial** \(x\)-term: \(-3.0492\,x e^{-|x|}\), involving **\(\exp(-|x|)\)** (absolute value is essential; \(x\) can be negative).
- No dependence on \(t\).

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1тАУ16 (pure polynomials in \(x\), \(v\); no trig/exp/abs)
All of 1тАУ16 are sums of monomials like \(x^k\), \(v\), \(v^3\), \(v x^2\), constants, etc.  
- None contains \(\sin(v)\) (or any trig), so they cannot reproduce the GTтАЩs \(-0.1430\sin(v)\) term unless that term were zero (it is not).
- None contains \(\exp(-|x|)\), so they cannot reproduce \(-3.0492\,x e^{-|x|}\) as a global identity (a polynomial cannot equal \(x e^{-|x|}\) for all real \(x\)).
Therefore **1тАУ16 cannot match**.

### Candidate 17 (adds \( \cos(c8 t)\))
Still no \(\sin(v)\) and no \(\exp(-|x|)\). Also introduces \(t\)-dependence unless coefficient set to 0, but even then missing required GT terms. **No match**.

### Candidate 18 (has \(t x\) and \(t(c8+v)^5\))
No \(\sin(v)\), no \(\exp(-|x|)\). Also \(t\)-dependence unless zeroed; still canтАЩt create required non-polynomial/trig-in-\(v\) structure. **No match**.

### Candidate 19тАУ22 (polynomial/rational-free; some include \(t x\))
No \(\sin(v)\), no \(\exp(-|x|)\). Any \(t\) terms can be zeroed but missing required structures. **No match**.

### Candidate 23 (includes \(\log(c6 x+1)\))
Has a non-polynomial (log) but GT needs \(\exp(-|x|)\) specifically and also needs \(\sin(v)\). Log cannot be tuned to equal \(x e^{-|x|}\) for all real \(x\), and still no \(\sin(v)\). **No match**.

### Candidate 24тАУ29 (various polynomials + extra \(t\)/powers)
None has \(\sin(v)\) or \(\exp(-|x|)\). **No match**.

### Candidate 30 (has \(\sin(c3 v + c4)\))
This is the only place (besides 46/50) with trig in \(v\). We can phase/scale to match \(\sin(v)\): set \(c3=1\), \(c4=0\), \(c2=-0.1430477510\). Good.

There is **no way** to produce the factor \(e^{-|x|}\) or the absolute value dependence using only algebraic powers. So even though the \(\sin(v)\) part can match, the \(x\exp(-|x|)\) term cannot. **No match**.

### Candidate 31тАУ34 (polynomial forms)
No \(\sin(v)\), no \(\exp(-|x|)\). **No match**.

### Candidate 35тАУ39 (include rational-in-\(t\) terms like \(v/(c7+t)\))

**GT:** `-0.194830767863936*v*(1 - x**2) - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

Expanding: `-0.194830767863936*v + 0.194830767863936*v*x**2 - 3.04923978373096*x*exp(-Abs(x)) - 0.143047751034959*sin(v)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v` (linear in v)
2. `v*x**2` 
3. `x*exp(-Abs(x))` 
4. `sin(v)`

The key challenge is that `x*exp(-Abs(x))` and `sin(v)` are specific transcendental functions. Let me analyze which candidates could match.

**Critical observations:**
- `x*exp(-Abs(x))` is NOT a polynomial in x. No finite polynomial (x, x┬│, xтБ╡, x^c) can exactly equal `x*exp(-Abs(x))` for all x.
- `sin(v)` is NOT a polynomial in v. No finite polynomial (v, v┬│) can exactly equal `sin(v)` for all v.
- Terms like `x**c` with fractional c cannot reproduce `x*exp(-Abs(x))` either.

Let me check candidates with `sin(v)` or similar:

**Candidate 30:** `c0*x + c1*x**5 + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*x**c6 + c7*v + c8*v*x**2`

Since `x*exp(-Abs(x))` cannot be represented as any finite sum of power-law terms `x^a`, polynomial terms, logarithmic terms, or trigonometric terms, **none of the candidates can match the GT**.

Let me verify: Could `c1*x^c2 + c3*x^c4` somehow equal `x*exp(-|x|)`? No - `x*exp(-|x|)` is not a sum of power laws. Power laws have the form `x^a` which are monotonic for x>0 (or have specific symmetry), while `x*exp(-|x|)` has a maximum and decays to 0, which no finite sum of power laws can replicate exactly.
